<span id="freeTextContainer12661832281759017016">Cohen the Barbarian.He's been a legend in his own lifetime.He can remember the good old days of high adventure, when being a Hero meant one didn't have to worry about aching backs and lawyers and civilization.But these days, he can't always remember just where he put his teeth...So now, with his ancient (yet still trusty) sword and new walking stick in hand, Cohen gathers</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12661832281759017016">Cohen the Barbarian.He's been a legend in his own lifetime.He can remember the good old days of high adventure, when being a Hero meant one didn't have to worry about aching backs and lawyers and civilization.But these days, he can't always remember just where he put his teeth...So now, with his ancient (yet still trusty) sword and new walking stick in hand, Cohen gathers a group of his old -- very old -- friends to embark on one final quest. He's going to climb the highest mountain of Discworld and meet the gods.It's time the Last Hero in the world returns what the first hero stole. Trouble is, that'll mean the end of the world, if no one stops him in time.</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1457841734">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer140673398305992340">Este es uno de los libros que me ha gustado del mundodisco, por varias razones, no solo tiene al cobarde de <strong>Rincewind</strong> <u>salvando al mundo una vez mas</u>, aunque el solo quisiera huir y/o esconderse; sino que tiene una cofradía de personajes de todo el disco, tenemos a todo <strong>El cuadro académico de la ilustre universidad invisible</strong>, al Patricio de Ankh-Morpork <strong>Lord Vetinari</strong>, al <strong>Capitán Zanahoria</strong> de la guardia de la ciudad, a <strong>La muerte</strong> (que no podría faltar) y lo mejor de todo a <strong>la Horda de plata</strong> <br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1450155483i/17386717.jpg" /><br /><br />Este gru</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText140673398305992340">Este es uno de los libros que me ha gustado del mundodisco, por varias razones, no solo tiene al cobarde de <strong>Rincewind</strong> <u>salvando al mundo una vez mas</u>, aunque el solo quisiera huir y/o esconderse; sino que tiene una cofradía de personajes de todo el disco, tenemos a todo <strong>El cuadro académico de la ilustre universidad invisible</strong>, al Patricio de Ankh-Morpork <strong>Lord Vetinari</strong>, al <strong>Capitán Zanahoria</strong> de la guardia de la ciudad, a <strong>La muerte</strong> (que no podría faltar) y lo mejor de todo a <strong>la Horda de plata</strong> <br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1450155483i/17386717.jpg" /><br /><br />Este grupo de viejitos cool que sigue a <strong>Cohen el bárbaro</strong>, quien tiene el plan de una última misión, devolverle lo que le pertenece a los dioses, lo primero que los mortales le robaron, el problema es que se lo quieren pagar con intereses, y debido a esto puede que todo el mundodisco se destruya.<br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1450155692i/17386743.jpg" /><br /><br />Me gustaron las ilustraciones del libro, todas son fantásticas <br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380334544i/693821.jpg" /><br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1450155483i/17386719._SY540_.jpg" /><br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1400702021i/9710000._SX540_.jpg" /><br /><br />Y una de las cosas que más me encanto, es que, a pesar de ser una historia cortita, tiene un inicio un desarrollo y un cierre <s>con Pratchett esto no sucede todo el tiempo</s> y ese final fue esplendido, todo un bombazo, de los mejores, así que los invito a acompañar a Rincewind a otra de sus aventuras peligrosas - <em>lo siento Rincewind por más que no lo quieras como tú mismo lo dices así es tu vida</em> <br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1450155483i/17386720.jpg" /><br /></span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_932391482">

  <a href="/user/show/5293536-melki" class="left imgcol" title="Melki"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1308071306p2/5293536.jpg" alt="Melki" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/932391482?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 21, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5293536-melki" class="user" title="Melki">Melki</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/34503.The_Last_Hero" title="Paperback 9780060507770" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/5293536-melki?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5293536-melki?shelf=humorous-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">humorous-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer932391482">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1964621482358246707"><strong>'And the thing is...the <em>big</em> thing about Cohen is...he's contagious.'<br /><br />'You mean he's a plague carrier?'<br /><br />'It's like a mental illness, sir. Or magic. He's as crazy as a stoat, but...once they've been around him for a while, people start seeing the world the way he does. All big and simple and they want to be part of it.'</strong><br /><br />This must be how Cohen the Barbarian got his Silver Horde to follow him up the highest mountain in Discworld to return something that was stolen from the Gods. BUT - for reasons too c</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1964621482358246707"><strong>'And the thing is...the <em>big</em> thing about Cohen is...he's contagious.'<br /><br />'You mean he's a plague carrier?'<br /><br />'It's like a mental illness, sir. Or magic. He's as crazy as a stoat, but...once they've been around him for a while, people start seeing the world the way he does. All big and simple and they want to be part of it.'</strong><br /><br />This must be how Cohen the Barbarian got his Silver Horde to follow him up the highest mountain in Discworld to return something that was stolen from the Gods. BUT - for reasons too complicated to go into here, it will mean the end of the world if he succeeds. So, it's up to Carrot, Rincewind and Leonard of Quirm to stop him, and...OH, YE GODS! The <s>stewardess</s> Librarian is flying the plane! <br /><br /><strong>'Ook!' said the Librarian.<br /><br />'He says we'll have to land soon,' said Carrot. 'Was there some position we're supposed to get into?'<br /><br />'Ook!' said the Librarian. He seemed to be fighting the levers.<br /><br />'What do you mean, "Lie on your back with your arms folded across your chest"?'</strong><br /><br />There's really only enough material here for a short story, Discworld Lite, if you will, but there's still plenty to enjoy. Meeting the Gods was fun. I LOVE that there is a God of Unnecessary Paperwork and a Goddess of Certain Types of Ice Cream and Short Lengths of String.<br /><br />I rate the story a three. It didn't really hold my interest, though to be fair, I am ruled by the Goddess of the Easily Distracted. I found myself rushing through the text to get to more of the gorgeous artwork. <br /><br />Just feast your eyes on some of these beauties:<br /><br /><img width="400" height="256" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1400702021i/9710000._SX540_.jpg" /><br /><br /><img width="400" height="280" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1400702021i/9710001.jpg" /><br /><br /><img width="354" height="465" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1400702021i/9710002._SY540_.jpg" /><br /><br /><img width="365" height="416" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1400702021i/9710003.jpg" /><br /><br />There you have it. A fun time, loads to look at, but a necessary read only for Discworld completists. But do borrow the book JUST to look at the pictures! Drool!</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="1964621482358246707">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_86915673">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/86915673" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/922495-patrick" class="left imgcol" title="Patrick"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1351307095p2/922495.jpg" alt="Patrick" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/86915673?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 08, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/922495-patrick" class="user" title="Patrick">Patrick</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/34503.The_Last_Hero" title="Paperback 9780060507770" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer86915673">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12971961442402237874">This was the the last book on Terry Pratchett re-read binge. <br /><br />While not as substantial as some of the rest of his books (I'm pretty sure the wordcount is less than half of his usual) this book makes up for it by being beautifully illustrated by Paul Kidby. I've never seen an artist do such spot-on interpretations of an author's characters. Kidby's work is really amazing. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/365349678" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/4720883-s-a" class="left imgcol" title="S.A."><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1364447630p2/4720883.jpg" alt="S.A." /></a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/365349678?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 11, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4720883-s-a" class="user" title="S.A.">S.A.</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/1938308.The_Last_Hero" title="Paperback 9780575081963" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer365349678">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10678852332687799536">I found this slim book tucked away behind other books. I think I hid it like a last bottle of really excellent wine. <br /><br />This time the sassy, wonderful, snide, silly, colorful, twisted thingamabobs associated with Sir Terry's wordsmithery are augmented by Paul Kidby's frantic illustrations. What a visual and verbal banquet. In my volume, page 130-131 is particularly enchanting.<br /><br />It's hard to pick a favorite character in Sir Terry's pantheon, but damn, Lord Vetinari, the cultivated, calculating, well-m</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10678852332687799536">I found this slim book tucked away behind other books. I think I hid it like a last bottle of really excellent wine. <br /><br />This time the sassy, wonderful, snide, silly, colorful, twisted thingamabobs associated with Sir Terry's wordsmithery are augmented by Paul Kidby's frantic illustrations. What a visual and verbal banquet. In my volume, page 130-131 is particularly enchanting.<br /><br />It's hard to pick a favorite character in Sir Terry's pantheon, but damn, Lord Vetinari, the cultivated, calculating, well-mannered tyrant, is ahead by a finely arched nostril.<br /><br />I read the last few pages weeping while grinning like a loon. When Sir Terry's words tickle me in all the correct places, bring on the cliche laugh and cry.<br /><br />Heroes never die. And if they do, for fucks sake don't tell them! Just feed them walrus stew and let them ride with the wind.<br /><br />Brilliant.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="10678852332687799536">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_196191347">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/196191347" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/5743748-wastrel" class="left imgcol" title="Wastrel"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1317660831p2/5743748.jpg" alt="Wastrel" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/196191347?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 01, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5743748-wastrel" class="user" title="Wastrel">Wastrel</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/34540.The_Last_Hero" title="Hardcover 9780575068858" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/5743748-wastrel?shelf=r-ss" class="actionLinkLite">r-ss</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5743748-wastrel?shelf=z-2001" class="actionLinkLite">z-2001</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5743748-wastrel?shelf=fantastika-unbounded-fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantastika-unbounded-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer196191347">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13689825604374426918">An installment that it's very easy to overlook: it's only a very short illustrated novel, after all. More a lengthy short story than a novel, to be honest. And when you think about the plot, the characters and so on, it's all very simple, very small, nothing all that impressive.<br /><br />But the flip side of that is that there's no room for most of Pratchett's vices. Combine that tight focus with an author at the peak of his powers, and the result is near-perfect execution. The comic bits are very funny,</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13689825604374426918">An installment that it's very easy to overlook: it's only a very short illustrated novel, after all. More a lengthy short story than a novel, to be honest. And when you think about the plot, the characters and so on, it's all very simple, very small, nothing all that impressive.<br /><br />But the flip side of that is that there's no room for most of Pratchett's vices. Combine that tight focus with an author at the peak of his powers, and the result is near-perfect execution. The comic bits are very funny, the tragic bits are very moving, the themes are clear and powerful. The art varies from 'mediocre' through to 'exceptional'. And it feels like a big farewell to a well-loved older incarnation of the series - many themes are shared with 'Troll Bridge' and <em>Interesting Times</em>, but the story is obviously much bigger than 'Troll Bridge', and much more succesful than <em>Interesting Times</em>. You could argue that there've very little said here that Pratchett hasn't said already, and that's probably why I get a feeling of lightness from it, and why people forget about it. But I'll say again: the execution is very close to perfect. This absolutely should not be dismissed as something second-rate, except in length and complexity. It's a small, minor, easily-overlooked brilliant little gem of a book.<br /><br />My fuller review is over at <a>my blog</a>.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13689825604374426918">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_440007412">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/440007412" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/4056309-ashish" class="left imgcol" title="Ashish"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1283703985p2/4056309.jpg" alt="Ashish" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/440007412?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 22, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4056309-ashish" class="user" title="Ashish">Ashish</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/4056309-ashish?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4056309-ashish?shelf=humour" class="actionLinkLite">humour</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer440007412">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2510972946916767936"><em>"So many worlds. So little time."</em><br />In the course of the last 26 books, Pratchett gave us a brilliant cast of characters. We've watched them appear, grow, evolve, and become a part of the Discworld Universe; Cohen was the only one who was who he was, in the beginning and till the end. That's what defined him, and that's what also, I thought, made him increasingly irrelevant in a Discworld with high-speed communications, reformed and societally-assimilated monsters, the rule of law &amp; order and,</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2510972946916767936"><em>"So many worlds. So little time."</em><br />In the course of the last 26 books, Pratchett gave us a brilliant cast of characters. We've watched them appear, grow, evolve, and become a part of the Discworld Universe; Cohen was the only one who was who he was, in the beginning and till the end. That's what defined him, and that's what also, I thought, made him increasingly irrelevant in a Discworld with high-speed communications, reformed and societally-assimilated monsters, the rule of law &amp; order and, most of all, a full map. There were no more uncharted forests, misty mountains, desolate icefields, and endless oceans. For a Hero who lived on the edge of everything, the complete civilization of the world was the end of final chapter of his life. <br />We thought there were no more surprises left. <br /><br /><strong>And he proved us spectacularly wrong. </strong><br /><br />I can't help but see a touch of the autobiographical in this. A sense of nostalgia for a simpler, more mysterious, and vaster world. I don't know if it's symbolic that the last great discovery - the true mapping out of the world, above and below, also happens in this book; now that there are no more mysteries, Cohen's world is finally ended - but Cohen himself continues. He takes that final step into the only place left for him. <br />He becomes Legend. <br />And the song lives on, though the singer is forgotten. <br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2510972946916767936">...more</a>

          </span>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer329376270">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11559135847763446520">I NEED TO OWN THIS BOOK ASAP. It has pictures! Of old men! And dragons! <br />Even without the illustrations, I'd buy it anyway.<br /><br />The Last Hero is technically a Rincewind book but it's mainly about Cohen &amp; The Silver Horde and Leonard of Quirm, served with a side of Carrot. It also has a bunch of other people. It's glorious. I loved Vena/Mrs. McGarry - one of the reasons I love Pratchett is because he writes awesome women. I <em>like</em> that Vena doesn't do much in the realm of swashbuckling, even though w</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11559135847763446520">I NEED TO OWN THIS BOOK ASAP. It has pictures! Of old men! And dragons! <br />Even without the illustrations, I'd buy it anyway.<br /><br />The Last Hero is technically a Rincewind book but it's mainly about Cohen &amp; The Silver Horde and Leonard of Quirm, served with a side of Carrot. It also has a bunch of other people. It's glorious. I loved Vena/Mrs. McGarry - one of the reasons I love Pratchett is because he writes awesome women. I <em>like</em> that Vena doesn't do much in the realm of swashbuckling, even though we know that she's a legend. She chooses to be Mrs. McGarry. Well, mostly. (I would love to see Xena the Warrior Princess in old age, seriously.) And the minstrel is one of those characters that I'm defenseless against, ie. he's one of those sleazy/hapless ones who grow the most during the journey (in fact, he grows up to be Orpheus, haha). <br /><br />Honestly, the whole thing is just completely rewarding and emotional in a laughing-through-your-tears sort of way. AUGH. <blockquote>
<strong>BLIND IO:</strong> I feel that if we had wanted people to fly, we would have given them wings.<br /><strong>OFFLER:</strong> We allow broomthtickth and magic carpeth. <br /><strong>BLIND IO:</strong> Ah, but they're magical. Magic... religion... there is a certain association. <em>This</em> is an attempt to subvert the natural order. Just <em>anyone</em> could float around the place in one of these things. Men could look <em>down</em> upon their gods! Why did you do it? <br /><strong>LEONARD OF QUIRM:</strong> You gave me wings when you showed me birds. I just made what I saw.</blockquote> <br /><blockquote>
<strong>BLIND IO:</strong> Tell me. Is there a god of policemen?<br /><strong>CARROT:</strong> No, sir. Coppers would be far too suspicious of anyone calling themselves a god of policemen to believe in one.<br /><strong>BLIND IO:</strong> But you are a gods-fearing man?<br /><strong>CARROT:</strong> What I've seen of them certainly frightens the light out of me, sir. And my commander always says, when we go about our business in the city, that when you look at the state of mankind you are forced to accept the reality of the gods.</blockquote> <br /></span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1630205-myles?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1630205-myles?shelf=humor" class="actionLinkLite">humor</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer116027149">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14657724889175619106">Due to the large format of this book - which after reading I would never dream of having scaled down - it is not carried in many places; As I was too impatient to wait for it to come in on order, I instead had read it at the local library.<br /><br />The Last Hero is a great story, when long-standing characters are illustrated it often comes out wrong, but Kirby nailed it, especially with Rincewind and the Gods. <br /><br />The basic story is in two arcs, focusing on the aging Silver Hoard (last seen in Interesting Tim</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14657724889175619106">Due to the large format of this book - which after reading I would never dream of having scaled down - it is not carried in many places; As I was too impatient to wait for it to come in on order, I instead had read it at the local library.<br /><br />The Last Hero is a great story, when long-standing characters are illustrated it often comes out wrong, but Kirby nailed it, especially with Rincewind and the Gods. <br /><br />The basic story is in two arcs, focusing on the aging Silver Hoard (last seen in Interesting Times) traveling to the home of the gods and Leonard da Quirm, Captain Carrot and a reluctant Rincewind who must stop them. <br /><br />Pratchett spins off of the established ideas about heroes and villains, gods, and gives insight into their motivations and what might happen when heroes and villains grow old. <br /><br />The story is good, but the prize really goes to Paul Kirby for his illustrations from the full two-page spreads to the details of da Quirm's notebooks. <br /><br />All in all, very satisfying. </span>

  <a href="/user/show/10450738-matthew-lloyd" class="left imgcol" title="Matthew Lloyd"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1340559752p2/10450738.jpg" alt="Matthew Lloyd" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1449433319?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 26, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/10450738-matthew-lloyd" class="user" title="Matthew Lloyd">Matthew Lloyd</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/10450738-matthew-lloyd?shelf=discworld" class="actionLinkLite">discworld</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1449433319">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15220952050315440934">I had been thinking, following the death of Terry Pratchett and the release of <em> <a title="The Shepherd's Crown by Terry Pratchett" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25324129.The_Shepherd_s_Crown">The Shepherd's Crown</a> </em> this year, that I had but one Discworld book yet to read. But back in 2001, after the death of <a title="Josh Kirby" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/102571.Josh_Kirby">Josh Kirby</a>, there was one Discworld book that I could not bring myself to read. Before I had even begun to read the Discworld books, I had come to associate the Disc with the art of Kirby's detailed fantasy settings, the billowing robes of long-bearded wizzards, the bumpy bodies of the human figures, t</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15220952050315440934">I had been thinking, following the death of Terry Pratchett and the release of <em>
  <a title="The Shepherd's Crown by Terry Pratchett" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25324129.The_Shepherd_s_Crown">The Shepherd's Crown</a>
</em> this year, that I had but one Discworld book yet to read. But back in 2001, after the death of <a title="Josh Kirby" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/102571.Josh_Kirby">Josh Kirby</a>, there was one Discworld book that I could not bring myself to read. Before I had even begun to read the Discworld books, I had come to associate the Disc with the art of Kirby's detailed fantasy settings, the billowing robes of long-bearded wizzards, the bumpy bodies of the human figures, the candle-wax quality of the architecture. The artwork of Paul Kidby, which appeared on the diaries and some of the maps, just didn't quite compare. So, when <em>The Last Hero</em> appeared, I didn't read it. And somehow, more than a decade later, I hadn't managed to rectify that omission.<br /><br /><em>The Last Hero</em> is something of a conclusion, albeit to a version of the Discworld which came to an end at around the time Josh Kirby died. The fantasy tropes employed by Pratchett in the earliest Discworld books - the incompetent wizard Rincewind, the warrior Cohen the Barbarian, the gods - appear here as important characters for the last time. Even Captain Carrot, who would remain an important part of the City Watch, would be side-lined in favour of his Commander, Vimes, in future novels focusing on the Watch. The story presents itself as a "fable", but there is no particular change in style from the earlier Discworld stories; Pratchett's typical humour, puns, and characterization is right here, illustrated copiously by Paul Kidby. The story is fun - hardly a starting point, but certainly good if you want to get a feel for the world and, perhaps, how it looks. Pratchett, in all his pre-embuggerance glory (and flaws) is right here.<br /><br />I can't say that I have completely come around to Paul Kidby's art as <em>The</em> Discworld. While there is a little more individuality to the characters he draws than Kirby's, I find the long, thin, clean, white faces of everyone off-putting; I think his Disc and Great A'Tuin look (excuse the pun) flat and lacking in majesty. I would like to say that I tried to like it, but had this book been illustrated by Josh Kirby, I think I might have given it five stars.* Blame my childhood delight in those covers... but they remain the Discworld for me.<br /><br />* I haven't read <em>
  <a title="The Illustrated Eric (Discworld, #9) by Terry Pratchett" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7962617.The_Illustrated_Eric__Discworld___9_">The Illustrated Eric</a>
</em>, only the unillustrated editions, and perhaps that would give me an idea?</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="15220952050315440934">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer279781795">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10403883495941064922">Cohen the Barbarian and his troupe set off to return fire to the Gods, when their real plan is to set-off a bomb. Meanwhile, the Patrician organizes a team to thwart them, anchored by Leonard of Quirm, Captain Carrot, and Rincewind, which involves rocketing undenearth Discworld. Nicely illustrated, and good to see the characters from a number of Pratchett novels.</span>

          </span>

Normally, I'm no great fan of the Discworld-books featuring the wizards, but this one had me chuckling out loud. (Which is quite embarrassing and gets you an awful lot of strange looks when you're reading in a fully packed train.) Cohen and his cohorts belong in a geriatric centre, but decide to have on last adventure: returning the stolen fire to the gods. This would end the world of course, and Ankh-Morpork sends its best and brightest to t</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13224037239582330701">Rinzwind, the Librarian, Leonard and Carrot in space! Normally, I'm no great fan of the Discworld-books featuring the wizards, but this one had me chuckling out loud. (Which is quite embarrassing and gets you an awful lot of strange looks when you're reading in a fully packed train.) Cohen and his cohorts belong in a geriatric centre, but decide to have on last adventure: returning the stolen fire to the gods. This would end the world of course, and Ankh-Morpork sends its best and brightest to the rescue. That is Carrot (to arrest the lot), Rinzwind (because he knows Cohen) and Leonard da Quirm (because he knows how to get there).<br />Fast-paced, humoristic, and with the necessary winks to history and pop culture, The Last Hero deserves every star you can possibly give.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_933223494">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/933223494" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/17261852-katerina" class="left imgcol" title="Katerina"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1402325433p2/17261852.jpg" alt="Katerina" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/933223494?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 03, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/17261852-katerina" class="user" title="Katerina">Katerina</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/1938308.The_Last_Hero" title="Paperback 9780575081963" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/17261852-katerina?shelf=favorites" class="actionLinkLite">favorites</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/17261852-katerina?shelf=recensioni" class="actionLinkLite">recensioni</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/17261852-katerina?shelf=terry-pratchett" class="actionLinkLite">terry-pratchett</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/17261852-katerina?shelf=letture-in-inglese" class="actionLinkLite">letture-in-inglese</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer933223494">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16617856370041102948">Un libro di Terry Pratchett è sempre una garanzia ma ci sono volte che cominci con qualche riserva: The Last Hero è un libro illustrato di 176 pagine con, credo, un terzo delle parole che ci sono di solito.<br />Che sia brutto non te lo aspetti. Che sia meno... sì.<br />Ma Terry Pratchett è un genio e non dobbiamo mai, mai, dimenticarlo.<br /><br />A volte non riesco a non pensare a come avrei voluto conoscere Terry Pratchett durante la mia infanzia, e come i miei eventuali figli lo conosceranno durante la loro (se si</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16617856370041102948">Un libro di Terry Pratchett è sempre una garanzia ma ci sono volte che cominci con qualche riserva: The Last Hero è un libro illustrato di 176 pagine con, credo, un terzo delle parole che ci sono di solito.<br />Che sia brutto non te lo aspetti. Che sia meno... sì.<br />Ma Terry Pratchett è un genio e non dobbiamo mai, mai, dimenticarlo.<br /><br />A volte non riesco a non pensare a come avrei voluto conoscere Terry Pratchett durante la mia infanzia, e come i miei eventuali figli lo conosceranno durante la loro (se si spicciano a tradurlo, che di questo passo il progetto slitterà ai miei eventuali nipoti): questo è l'effetto che i libri di quest'uomo hanno su di me. Ho finito il libro e sono rimasta lì, senza sapere se essere triste o divertita o malinconica. <br />Ci sono motivi per essere tutto ciò, e non perchè il finale sia un pastrocchio. È perfetto.<br />Ma andiamo con ordine: siccome so che siamo circa in tre a leggere Pratchett (e uno Cohen ancora non l'ha incontrato), vi spiego: Cohen il Barbaro è un personaggio ricorrente di Mondo Disco nonchè dichiarata parodia di Conan il Barbaro, nonchè il più grande eroe che il Disco abbia mai avuto.<br />Cosa succede quando un personaggio del genere invecchia? Succede che abbiamo abbiamo la classica gag del personaggio completamente fuori posto, un pesce non fuor d'acqua ma proprio sparato nell'universo.<br />Ma siccome Pratchett non è scemo non si ferma lì e Cohen acquista una dimensione che, sotto il divertimento, sotto l'arguzia, sotto i giochi di parole che tanto gli vengono bene, ha discrete sfumature tragiche.<br /><br />Cohen è l'ultimo baluardo di un mondo semplice (e, a livello meta, della narrativa high fantasy) che non ha posto nel mondo moderno: i tempi sono cambiati, lui no. È fuori luogo in modo comico finchè non ti accorgi che lui lo sa, e che quando gli altri personaggi lo incontrano sono sempre un po' a disagio perchè Cohen dovrebbe essere morto ed essere una leggenda, non una leggenda vivente.<br />È sopravvissuto a tutto, incluso il suo tempo. Il loop in cui è intrappolato è ovvio: Pratchett considera la vecchiaia la somma della vita e Cohen è il migliore. Troppo esperto per morire in battaglia, troppo esperto per cadere in una trappola e non uscirne: gli è precluso morire in combattimento, lo stesso Morte sembra riluttante all'idea di andarlo a prendere (non che non lo farebbe: il dovere è il dovere), gli dei l'hanno dimenticato.<br />Il suo destino è morire sul letto, in un mondo che non lo apprezza più.<br />Cohen non ci sta. Cohen gioca d'anticipo e con la sua Silver Horde (più un menestrello rapito e l'ultimo Signore Oscuro) decide di scrivere la propria fine riportando il fuoco agli dei - con gli interessi - e restituendo all'umanità il libero arbitrio.<br /><br />Ma qual è la fregatura? Che Mondo Disco è una realtà così instabile che ha bisogno delle divinità e della magia per esistere... ed ecco quindi che il Patrizio, con l'aiuto dei maghi, organizza una missione per fermare gli arzilli vecchietti: Scuotivento, Carota e Leonardo da Quirm devono partire con un'astronave fatta di legno e alimentata a draghi (mezzo inventato apposta da Leonardo, e unica possibilità di raggiungerli in tempo) e far ragionare Cohen.<br />In sostanza gruppo di personaggi A cerca di raggiungere località Z mentre gruppo di personaggi B cerca di intercettarli.<br /><br />In questo libro vediamo la vecchiaia affrontata in modo diverso rispetto alle streghe: mentre loro con l'età migliorano per gli eroi il decadimento fisico è una vera e propria tortura. Sono stati quelli che hanno fatto tutto e si ritrovano senza nulla.<br />È interessante leggere come Cohen e gli altri continuino ad applicare alla loro vita le regole del Codice, ma contemporaneamente siano anche esperti abbastanza da guardare il mondo con consapevolezza e cinismo.<br /><em>They say fortune favours the brave, but <strong>I</strong> say I've seen too many brave men walkin' into battles they never walked out of.</em><br /><br />La cosa completamente assurda e geniale è che questi anziani signori sono così esperti nelle regole del loro stile di vita (e della loro narrazione) che sono in grado di uscire da determinate situazioni (o di riconoscerle) proprio perchè conoscono e sfruttano i clichè narrativi: capiscono di essere nel torto non tanto perchè glielo spiegano, ma perchè sono in sette contro uno che lotta per salvare il mondo.<br />Qualunque eroe vissuto abbastanza da avere ottanta-novant'anni sa di non avere nessuna possibilità di vittoria in uno scenario simile.<br />Più l'importanza della memoria: che senso hanno le imprese se non c'è nessuno a ricordarle?<br /><br />In questo libro si vedono gli dei per molto più tempo rispetto agli altri volumi (Tartarughe Divine parla più che altro di fede) e si riconferma l'impressione generale: creature potentissime ma infantili, che giocano letteralmente col destino degli uomini (ma giochi semplici perchè non hanno pazienza) e che possono scordarsi le loro pedine sul tavolo, o non pensare a cosa succede quando le fai arrivare fino alla fine del tabellone di gioco.<br />Ho trovato interessante come, nonostante loro vivano infinitamente più a lungo degli umani, siano più giovani rispetto a noi: in fin dei conti proprio perchè gli umani vivono meno invecchiano di più... e Pratchett è abbastanza bravo da riuscire ad usare una sola frase per mostrare questo concetto: quando Vena the Raven-Haired non uccide le valchirie perchè "they'd all looked so <em>young</em>". <br /><br />Non posso non sprecare una parola per i disegni di Paul Kidby: sono meravigliosi. Come ho avuto il libro in mano come ho desiderato averlo in copertina rigida, e quanto ho imprecato per le illustrazioni spaccate a metà dalla rilegature perchè in due pagine!<br />Moltissimi personaggi, e luoghi, sono esattamente come li ho sempre immaginati.<br /><br />Leggere questo libro è stata un'esperienza fantastica, non solo per la storia ma per come è stata scritta e per cosa rappresenta. Sono innumerevoli le frasi che meriterebbero di essere citate, o scritte e appese, i momenti 'Fuck yeah', la commozione per la fine di un'epoca, e ammiro come Pratchett abbia trovato un finale perfetto ad una situazione impossibile.<br />Mi ha fatto venir voglia di andare a cercare qualche vecchio amico: Conan, Solomon Kane, Elric, John Carter, Sandokan, per dirne qualcuno. Vecchi eroi messi in da parte perchè la narrativa è andata avanti e sono troppo semplici, basilari, per i gusti attuali.<br />Ma Scuotivento ha ragione.<br /><em>The thing is... the big thing about Cohen is... he's contagious. It's like a mental illness. Or magic. He's as crazy as a stoat, but... once they've been around him for a while, people start seeing the world as he does. All big and simple. And they want to be part of it.</em></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="16617856370041102948">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/48036167?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 03, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1805316-elise" class="user" title="Elise">Elise</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer48036167">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10296840851247369560">I didn't really like my first couple of experiences with Terry Pratchett. The first book I tried from Discworld was "The Color of Magic." I figured I start with it because it was the first book, but I was really disappointed with it and found it unfunny. I still wanted to give Discworld another chance though because I really wanted to like Terry Pratchett. So, I read around and found out that most people found his funniest book was "Guards! Guards!" So, I decided to buy it. I found it slightly b</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10296840851247369560">I didn't really like my first couple of experiences with Terry Pratchett. The first book I tried from Discworld was "The Color of Magic." I figured I start with it because it was the first book, but I was really disappointed with it and found it unfunny. I still wanted to give Discworld another chance though because I really wanted to like Terry Pratchett. So, I read around and found out that most people found his funniest book was "Guards! Guards!" So, I decided to buy it. I found it slightly better than "The Color of Magic," but I still found it only mildly amusing and still didn't get what the big deal of why these books are so popular. So, I swore off Pratchett for a while and decided that maybe he just wasn't my cup of tea.<br /><br />Now, for whatever reason I decided I wanted to try Pratchett again. This time I picked up "The Last Hero: A Discworld Fable." I have to say that this may very well be the first Pratchett book I actually enjoyed. Perhaps it was because it had more of a plot this time, or maybe it was because it was illustrated. The art in this book is very nice. But this time my visit to the Discworld was fun and entertaining. This time I actually found it amusing. The characters were all great, especially Cohen and his Horde. They were a really funny bunch. So, I gave Terry Pratchett another chance, and I'm glad I did.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="10296840851247369560">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8421652554949575238">This is a fun "fable" indeed. My kids love this one for the amazing illustrations. Not all of which I appreciate as much as they do. But the story is still a delight. I think it to be a perfect ending to Cohen the Barbarian. Pure Pratchett. Some favorite quotes:<br /><br />"The messages were in code, of course. If not examined too closely, it passes for justice."<br /><br />"Yes, but I've never understood what's wrong with the idea of being a coward. It takes guts to run away, you know. Lots of people would be as cowardly as me if they were brave enough."<br /><br />"If you believed in The Code, that was worrying. <span id="freeTextContainer17263286393552795922">It is impossible to rate just the story, because of the really really beautiful Kidby-pictures on almost every page (well, <em>every</em> page, the few pages without colour-pictures have nice background-images). I mean there are swamp-dragons, moon-dragons, kitties (actually: Death with a kitty, and a kitty playing with the Tail of the Death of Rats), the wizzards, and of course the heroes, the 'silver horde'. They are all awesome, and incredibly detailed, I want all of them as poster for my room XD.<br /><br />Now</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17263286393552795922">It is impossible to rate just the story, because of the really really beautiful Kidby-pictures on almost every page (well, <em>every</em> page, the few pages without colour-pictures have nice background-images). I mean there are swamp-dragons, moon-dragons, kitties (actually: Death with a kitty, and a kitty playing with the Tail of the Death of Rats), the wizzards, and of course the heroes, the 'silver horde'. Cohen is in company of his silver horde, and they're just an awesome bunch (Veena the Raven-Haired strangles someone with pink knitting-wool and stitched 'BURN THIS HOUSE DOWN' on fabric...how can you not love her?) and Rincewind get paired up with Carrot...you know I actually felt sorry for Rincewind, then.<br />Oh, and these pictures with Death and kitty? They illustrate a (somehow random) scene in which Death discusses Schroedinger's Cat with Albert. Don't tell me that's not awesome :)</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_145707486">

  <a href="/user/show/800291-andrew" class="left imgcol" title="Andrew"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1295167791p2/800291.jpg" alt="Andrew" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/145707486?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 24, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/800291-andrew" class="user" title="Andrew">Andrew</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/34503.The_Last_Hero" title="Paperback 9780060507770" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer145707486">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer562889974270947819">This book is one of the two large format books from the Discworld - (the other being Eric), however it is far more lavishly illustrated - this time by Paul KIdby - as this was published at the time of John Kirbys death. The illustrations are of a totally different style and although Kirby's style will be forever connected to the early Pratchett works I think these are just as good and compliment the story perfectly. <br />As for the story its quiet short considering the number of illustrations through</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText562889974270947819">This book is one of the two large format books from the Discworld - (the other being Eric), however it is far more lavishly illustrated - this time by Paul KIdby - as this was published at the time of John Kirbys death. The illustrations are of a totally different style and although Kirby's style will be forever connected to the early Pratchett works I think these are just as good and compliment the story perfectly. <br />As for the story its quiet short considering the number of illustrations throughout it - and is face paced and fun to read. The story possibly because of its length contains less of the footnote explanations (synonymous with Discworld) and just gets on with the story at hand. This was a fun read and at times a little cumbersome - it was highly enjoyable - i wont say anything about the story since like so many other characters it has an impact on the rest of the series on one shape or form and there are plenty of far better spoilers out there to give you the plotline. All in all a great book to read, </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="562889974270947819">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5479295538527928992">A diferencia de los libros que le preceden en la saga, Pratchett vuelve a sus orígenes en los que en lugar de analizar cómo un mundo fantástico se vuelve moderno, juega con lo que le queda de mágico. <br /><br />El Último Héroe satiriza los tópicos de las fantasías clásicas, en los héroes que ganan las batallas simplemente por ser los buenos, y lo condensa en una historia breve maravillosamente ilustrada por el gran Paul Kidby.<br /><br />Pese a lo simple de la historia, y lo metidos con calzador que están los personaj</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5479295538527928992">A diferencia de los libros que le preceden en la saga, Pratchett vuelve a sus orígenes en los que en lugar de analizar cómo un mundo fantástico se vuelve moderno, juega con lo que le queda de mágico. <br /><br />El Último Héroe satiriza los tópicos de las fantasías clásicas, en los héroes que ganan las batallas simplemente por ser los buenos, y lo condensa en una historia breve maravillosamente ilustrada por el gran Paul Kidby.<br /><br />Pese a lo simple de la historia, y lo metidos con calzador que están los personajes habituales (creo que solo para que Kidby tuviera una excusa para pintarlos), el libro entretiene y deja las perlas con las que Sir Terry siempre nos salpica sus novelas.<br /><br />Quizá como libro no da para más de tres estrellas o cuatro siendo generoso, pero la versión con las ilustraciones de Paul Kidby se merece las cinco estrellas sin la menor duda.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1302398830">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1302398830" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/33720863-will-ransohoff" class="left imgcol" title="Will Ransohoff"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1423686736p2/33720863.jpg" alt="Will Ransohoff" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1302398830?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 08, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/33720863-will-ransohoff" class="user" title="Will Ransohoff">Will Ransohoff</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/47992.The_Last_Hero" title="Paperback 9780575073777" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1302398830">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer20237530452701592">This book is a beautifully-illustrated attempt to write a fictional myth. It mixes the epic heroics of Greek mythology, the elegiac mood of Norse sagas, and the snappy writing and dialogue of modern fiction. I'm not sure what else to say about it, but as an experiment in mixing genres it works very well; its short length keeps the strange format from wearing out its welcome. I wish this sort of toying around with risky ideas and formats was more common.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1484067615">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1484067615?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 28, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/11715970-ian-banks" class="user" title="Ian Banks">Ian Banks</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/34540.The_Last_Hero" title="Hardcover 9780575068858" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/11715970-ian-banks?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/11715970-ian-banks?shelf=comedy" class="actionLinkLite">comedy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1484067615">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2322211193804609251"><p>This is a vehicle for the talents of Paul Kidby who was beginning to take over the cover illustration duty from the late and lamented Josh Kirby. It's similar in concept to <em>Eric</em>, which featured many of Mr Kirby's beautiful pictures as well. I've never been that fond of Mr Kidby's art, preferring his work as an idea rather than in the reality, but here he is terrific: the detail is extraordinary on many of the pictures and he knows how to grasp the essence of the characters, particularly when the</p></span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2322211193804609251"><p>This is a vehicle for the talents of Paul Kidby who was beginning to take over the cover illustration duty from the late and lamented Josh Kirby. It's similar in concept to <em>Eric</em>, which featured many of Mr Kirby's beautiful pictures as well. I've never been that fond of Mr Kidby's art, preferring his work as an idea rather than in the reality, but here he is terrific: the detail is extraordinary on many of the pictures and he knows how to grasp the essence of the characters, particularly when they have been fleshed out in the text. He pays attention.<br /></p><p>The story is brief: Cohen the Barbarian is sick of being old and decrepit and wants to give something back to the gods of Discworld: specifically, a bomb. Unfortunately, this will destroy the magic field that holds the Disc together (a callback to <em>Strata</em>, in which the proto-Discworld only functions through the application of vast amounts of energy). So the rest of the world sends a crack team to stop them, consisting of Leonard of Quirm; Captain Carrot of the Ankh-Morpork City Watch; and the person who knows Cohen best, Rincewind, Professor of Egregious Geography at Unseen University.<br /></p><p>They travel in a Discworld version of a rocket and have many adventures before arriving at Dunmanifestin, the home of the gods and their confrontation with Cohen.<br /></p><p>I really liked this: it's a throwback to the early Discworld , with Rincewind and Cohen, with lots of shoutouts to SF novels and movies, as well as the space programme, as well as some poignant observations about growing old and what we leave behind.<br /></p><p>Light but not slight.</p></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2322211193804609251">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1299860472">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1299860472" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/26064533-tulio-fernandez" class="left imgcol" title="Tulio Fernandez"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1385571612p2/26064533.jpg" alt="Tulio Fernandez" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1299860472?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 05, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/26064533-tulio-fernandez" class="user" title="Tulio Fernandez">Tulio Fernandez</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/6783223-el-ltimo-h-roe" title="Paperback 9788401337352" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1299860472">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7180270239991995224">El nombre de Terry Pratchett es mundialmente conocido por su saga de Mundodisco, ambientada en un mundo paralelo de fantasía el cual, y tal como su nombre lo indica, es un disco que está sostenido por cuatro elefantes apoyados en una tortuga gigante que avanza por el universo.<br /><br />En este mundo conviven magos, decanos, dioses de diferentes raleas, formas y sabores, conquistadores temibles, banqueros, bardos, orangutanes bibliotecarios y cualquier cosa que parece no tener sentido, en un maremágnum y c</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7180270239991995224">El nombre de Terry Pratchett es mundialmente conocido por su saga de Mundodisco, ambientada en un mundo paralelo de fantasía el cual, y tal como su nombre lo indica, es un disco que está sostenido por cuatro elefantes apoyados en una tortuga gigante que avanza por el universo.<br /><br />En este mundo conviven magos, decanos, dioses de diferentes raleas, formas y sabores, conquistadores temibles, banqueros, bardos, orangutanes bibliotecarios y cualquier cosa que parece no tener sentido, en un maremágnum y caos de tal magnitud que al empezar a leerlo, uno no puede dejar de preguntarse ¿Dónde habían estado estos libros durante toda mi vida?<br /><br />A pesar de no comenzar con el primer libro de la saga, Los colores de la magia, escrito en 1983, creo que empecé con el libro indicado: El último héroe, te ubica rápidamente en Mundodisco, en su mitología, sus personajes principales, en la magia que impregna cada una de sus páginas con una narrativa llena de humor tanto para grandes como chicos –es decir sin considerar a los niños como idiotas como si lo hacen otras lecturas-.<br /><br />En esta aventura nos muestran dos bandos. En uno se encuentra Cohen, el bárbaro y su equipo de conquistadores de la tercera edad quienes van en busca de los dioses para vengarse por haberlos hecho envejecer, es el prototipo de la aventura clásica –de espada en mano-; mientras que por otro lado tenemos a los representantes de la Escuela de magia: el mago Ricewind, Leonardo Da Quirm y el soldado Zanahoria quienes deben detenerlos usando un cohete espacial, acá se ve más una aventura de exploración, de ciencia ficción, de aventura al estilo Julio Verne. Más allá de ellos, están los dioses, quienes observan la situación y para quienes somos un simple divertimento.<br /><br />Es interesante observar las miles de referencias culturales que hace Pratchett en su obra. Es así como Cohen el bárbaro, nos remite a Conán; Leonardo Da Quirm es una copia exacta a Leonardo Da Vinci, los dioses son un batiburrillo del Olimpo y los dioses egipcios, a la vez que se alimenta de mitos como el de Prometeo, el gato de Shrödinger.<br /><br />Cabe destacar las ilustraciones de Paul Kidby. Debo confesar que en materia de libros soy más dado a la parte escrita que a la gráfica, y a diferencia de muchos amigos, que un libro tenga o no dibujos carece de importancia, pero en este caso los gráficos son hermosos, complementan de manera perfecta la historia y le dan un valor único a este tomo. <br /><br />A la largo de las páginas y en una historia que es aparentemente sencilla, el autor nos muestra reflexiones sobre la mortalidad, la vejez, los caprichos de los dioses, la moralidad y la eternidad del arte, la palabra y la música que quizá otros libros en apariencia más solemnes y serios serían incapaces de igualar. Además es más atractivo pensar sobre estos temas con una sonrisa en los labios que releyendo mil veces un denso párrafo para saber si se entendió ¿no?<br /><br />¿Quieren magia? ¿Quiéren diversión? ¿Humor a raudales? ¿Un orangután manejando un cohete espacial sobre un mundo sostenido por una tortuga gigante? Este libro es para ustedes. Por mi parte debo decir que el señor Pratchett acaba de ganar un fan incondicional que está dispuesto a iniciar la aventura que va por los 39 libros que conforman la saga. El viaje apenas comienza :D<br /><br /><br />Algunos apartes…<br /><br />En lo alto de la montaña, mientras se acercaban las ventiscas, hubo un resplandor rojizo en la nieve, siguió allí todo el invierno, y cuando soplaron las galernas primaverales los rubíes centellearon bajo el sol.<br />Nadie recuerda al cantante. La canción perdura.<br /><br />---<br /><br />Zanahoria negó tristemente con la cabeza.<br />-Tal vez podríamos bajar a mirar.<br />-¡Haría falta un milagro!- estalló Ricewind<br />-Siempre queda la esperanza.<br />-¿Y qué? Siempre quedan también los impuestos. Eso no cambia nada.<br /><br />---<br /><br />Forma parte de la naturaleza de las cosas que quienes salvan al mundo de una destrucción segura a menudo no reciben una recompensa enorme porque, como al final, no se produce la destrucción segura, la gente no está tan convencida de cuán de segura habría sido, y por lo tanto se muestran un poco reacios a la hora de repartir algo más sustancial que simples elogios.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="7180270239991995224">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_931838847">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/931838847" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/7173780-michael-clemens" class="left imgcol" title="Michael Clemens"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1442619474p2/7173780.jpg" alt="Michael Clemens" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/931838847?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 11, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/7173780-michael-clemens" class="user" title="Michael Clemens">Michael Clemens</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/34503.The_Last_Hero" title="Paperback 9780060507770" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer931838847">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6813633391586037434">Eternal coward Rincewind takes a welcome back seat to this sendoff to Cohen the Barbarian and his silver hoarde. The art enlivens a very short tale, too short, in fact, as there are many points at which it feels that Pratchett's prose is constrained by the format of the book -- a scene ends rapidly and is followed by a two-page art.<br /><br />And the art: by and large, very enjoyable, and even jibes with my mental image of how some of the characters "should" look, which is a testament I suppose to Sir Terr</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6813633391586037434">Eternal coward Rincewind takes a welcome back seat to this sendoff to Cohen the Barbarian and his silver hoarde. The art enlivens a very short tale, too short, in fact, as there are many points at which it feels that Pratchett's prose is constrained by the format of the book -- a scene ends rapidly and is followed by a two-page art.<br /><br />And the art: by and large, very enjoyable, and even jibes with my mental image of how some of the characters "should" look, which is a testament I suppose to Sir Terry's robust descriptions. Some of the character portraits are are little too comically done (e.g. bug-eyed) for my tastes. I think the humor of the Disc shines through best when it's played entirely straight, with the situations and the characters left to handle the heavy lifting of the jokes. It's a minor quibble, though. A too-quick read that colors in more of the history of the Disc without being a vital piece of backstory <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[and providing just the right sort of heroic sendoff for Cohen and his band. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--></span>

      <a href="/user/show/49228646-widad-oteh" class="user" title="Widad Oteh">Widad Oteh</a>

        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a href="/review/list/49228646-widad-oteh?shelf=favorites" class="actionLinkLite">favorites</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1463141889">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer125090041238140330">The Last Hero is extraordinarily good. I don't reread it half as often as some of my favourites, but whenever I do, I always wonder why I don't. Probably because it's too big to conveniently fit into a handbag, but I can be romantic and say it's to preserve the magic inside it. <br /><br />Vetinari is really very good in this. He plays one of his most active roles in protecting the Disc and it is glorious. Whenever I need to remember why I love him, I only need to read a few of his lines in The Last Hero an</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText125090041238140330">The Last Hero is extraordinarily good. I don't reread it half as often as some of my favourites, but whenever I do, I always wonder why I don't. Probably because it's too big to conveniently fit into a handbag, but I can be romantic and say it's to preserve the magic inside it. <br /><br />Vetinari is really very good in this. He plays one of his most active roles in protecting the Disc and it is glorious. Whenever I need to remember why I love him, I only need to read a few of his lines in The Last Hero and I'm grinning like a besotted schoolgirl. It's probably one of his best books, and therefore one of my favourites.<br /><br />Not that Vetinari is the only good thing in this book, of course. The illustrations only serve to confirm my views of the Disc, the Wizards are so wonderfully wizardly, Ponder is a dear, as usual, and there is so much wisdom in Cohen's story. This is a real hero's story - even though the two heroic groups are at conflict with each other and the gods are not particularly happy about it. Far too clever of a book to pass up for any excuse. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="125090041238140330">...more</a>
